First wipe the affected area until red, then roast the wrapped paste, using the heat to induce sweating, wrap it with cotton clothing, avoiding wind, until healing is achieved. [From "General Record"][109p]

　　治风(疒咅)(疒畾)：牛膝散。用牛膝酒浸捣为末，每服二钱，食前温酒调下；兼治骨疽风癞，皆效。
　　　　针灸

　　《素问》 【《素问》　原作《灵枢经》，据《素问》卷十四长刺节论改。】曰：病大风，骨节重，须眉堕，名曰大风。刺肌肉为故，汗出百日。刺骨髓，汗出百日。凡二百日，须眉生而止针。　　疠风者，素刺其肿上，已刺，以锐针针其处，按出其恶气，肿尽乃止。常食方食，勿食他食。　　《卫生宝鉴》曰：《内经》曰：脉风成疠。又云：风气与太阳俱入行诸脉俞，散分肉之间，卫气相干，其道不利，故使肉膹胀而有伤；卫气有所凝而不行，故肌肉不仁也。夫疠风者，有荣卫热胕，其气不清，故使鼻柱坏而色败，皮肤疡(疒贵)，风寒客于脉不去，名曰疠风，或名曰寒热病。[110p]

Treating Wind (疾病): Niu Xi Powder. Soak and pound Niu Xi in wine into a powder. Take two qian before meals, mixed with warm wine; it also treats bone sores, wind leprosy, all with effect.

Acupuncture

The "Suwen" says: For serious wind diseases, if the bones and joints are heavy, and the hair falls out, it is called “great wind.” Acupuncture of the muscles leads to sweat for a hundred days. Acupuncture of the bone marrow also leads to sweat for a hundred days. Overall, for two hundred days, once the hair grows back, stop acupuncture. For pestilential wind, one should first needle the swellings, and after needling, use a sharp needle to puncture that area to press out the bad qi, stopping only when the swelling is gone. Regularly consume regular food, and avoid other foods. The "Hygiene Treasure Mirror" cites: The "Neijing" states: Wind leads to pestilence. Moreover, it says: The wind energy and the sun enter the pathways of the meridians, dispersing among the muscles, interfering with the protective qi, leading to swelling and harm in the flesh; because the protective qi becomes stagnant and doesn’t circulate, the muscles become numb. Pestilential wind involves the warming and protecting influence being not clear, leading to ruin of the nasal columns and discoloration, skin ulcers, and cold and wind residing in the meridians without dissolution, named pestilential wind, or named cold-heat disease.[110p]

大风之病，骨节重，眉鬓堕，名曰大风，刺其肌肉，故汗出百日，刺骨髓汗出百日，凡二百日鬓眉生而止针。　　《景岳全书》曰：疠疡砭刺之法，张子和谓一汗抵千针，盖以砭血不如发汗之周遍也。然发汗即出血，出血即发汗，二者一也。若恶血凝滞在肌表经络者，宜刺委中出血则效。若恶毒蕴结于脏腑，非荡涤其内，则不能瘥。若毒在外者，非砭刺遍身患处，及两臂腿腕两手足指缝各出血，其毒必不能散。若表里俱受毒者，非外砭内泄，其毒决不能退。若上体多，宜用醉仙散，取其恶血从齿缝中出，及刺手指缝并臂腕，以去肌表毒血。若下体多，宜用再造散，令恶血陈虫，从谷道中出；仍针足指缝并腿腕，隔一二日更刺之，以血赤为度。如有恶热头痛等证，以大补气血为主。[111p]

The affliction known as "Great Wind" causes heaviness in the joints, drooping of the eyebrows and hair, and is named "Great Wind" because it pierces the muscles. Thus, sweating occurs for a hundred days, and piercing the bone marrow causes sweating for a hundred days as well, totaling two hundred days until the hair and eyebrows grow back and the needling ceases.

In the "Complete Book of Jingyue" it is stated: the method of using acupuncture for pestilential sores, Zhang Zihe said that a single sweat is worth a thousand needles, for acupuncture draws blood less effectively than sweating does in a comprehensive manner. Nevertheless, sweating leads to blood loss, and blood loss leads to sweating; they are one and the same. If the stagnant toxic blood accumulates on the surface of the muscles and meridians, it is advisable to puncture the Weizhong point to draw out blood for efficacy. If the toxic accumulation resides in the internal organs, it cannot heal without cleansing it from within. If the poison is located externally, not only must the diseased areas be needled, but blood must be drawn from the seams of the arms, legs, hands, and feet, for the toxin cannot disperse. If both the interior and exterior are poisoned, without external needling to draw out the internal toxins, it cannot possibly retreat.

If the upper body is more affected, it is suitable to use "Drunken Immortal Powder" to expel the toxic blood from between the teeth and to pierce the seams of the fingers and along the arms to remove the superficial toxic blood. If the lower body is more affected, it is appropriate to use "Restorative Powder" to allow the toxic blood and lingering parasites to emerge from the digestive tract; along with this, needling the seams of the toes and wrists should be done, with a gap of one or two days between sessions, using the color of the blood as a measure. If there are symptoms of toxic heat and headaches, the primary focus should be on greatly replenishing qi and blood.[111p]

　　　　医案

　　《儒门事亲》曰：朱葛解家病癞疾，求治于戴人，戴人辞之，待五六月间可治之时也。今春初尚寒，未可服药，我已具行装到宛丘，待五六月制药。朱解家以为托辞。后戴人果以六月间到朱葛，乃具大蒜、浮萍等药，使人召解家曰：药已成矣，可来就治。解为他药所惑，竞不至。戴人曰：向日非托辞也，以春寒未可发汗，暑月易发汗，针同发汗也。但无药者用针，一汗可抵千针。故高供奉采萍歌曰：不居山兮不在岸，采我之时七月半，选甚瘫风与痪风，些小微风都不算，豆淋酒内下三丸，铁幞头上也出汗。噫！文士相轻，医士相疾。文士不过自损，医士至于害人，其解家之谓欤？[112p]

Medical Case

The "Rujun Shiqin" states: Zhu Ge treated his family's leprosy and sought help from Dai, who declined, saying it would be treatable in five to six months. This spring, it was still cold, and medicine could not yet be taken; I had already prepared my travel gear to Wanqiu, waiting to concoct the medicine in five to six months. Zhu Ge believed this to be an excuse. Later, Dai indeed arrived at Zhu Ge in June, prepared garlic, duckweed, and other medicines, instructing someone to summon Zhu Ge, saying: "The medicine is ready, you may come for treatment." Zhu Ge, bewildered by other medicines, did not go. Dai remarked: "It was not an excuse before; in early spring, sweating was not possible due to the cold, but in the hotter months, it is easier to sweat. Acupuncture is the same as inducing sweat. However, for those without medicine, acupuncture can achieve the same effect as a thousand needles. Thus, Gao Gongfeng sang the tune of gathering duckweed: 'Not in the mountains, not on the shores, gather me in mid-July, distinguishing between paralysis wind and weakness wind; minor breezes do not count. Drop three pills in bean wine, the iron cap will also result in sweating.' Alas! Scholars belittle each other, physicians harm each other. Scholars merely incur self-damage, whereas physicians can harm others—such is the plight of Zhu Ge, isn’t it?[112p]

　　阳夏张主簿病癞十余年，眉发皆落，皮肤皴濇如树皮。戴人断之曰：是有汗者可治之，当大发汗，其汗出当臭，其涎当腥。乃置燠室中，遍塞风隙，以三圣散吐之，汗出周身，如卧水中，其汗果粘臭不可闻，痰皆腥如鱼涎，两足心微有汗；次以舟车丸、浚川散大下五七行，如此数次乃瘳。[113p]

In the summer of Yangxia, the registrar Zhang had suffered from leprosy for over ten years, losing all his hair and having skin as rough as tree bark. A diagnostic healer determined that it was treatable and advised to induce a great sweat. The sweat was supposed to be foul-smelling and the saliva fishy. They placed him in a heated room, sealing all gaps against drafts, and administered the San Sheng powder to induce vomiting. Sweat poured from his body as if he were in water, and indeed, the sweat was so thick and stinky it was unbearable. The phlegm was fishy like fish excrement, and the soles of his feet were slightly sweaty. Subsequently, they administered the Zhou Che pill and Jun Chuan powder to purge him vigorously five to seven times; after several such treatments, he was cured.[113p]

　　《卫生宝鉴》曰：戊寅岁正月，段库使病大风，满面连颈极痒，眉毛已脱落，须以热汤沃之则稍缓，昼夜数次沃之，或砭刺亦缓。先师曰：脉风者，疠风也。荣卫热胕，其气不清，故使鼻柱坏，皮肤色败。大风者，风寒客于脉而不去，治之当刺其肿上，以锐针针其处，按出其恶气，肿尽乃止。常食方食，勿食他食。
　　《薛己医案》曰：一男子冬间口苦耳鸣，阴囊湿痒，来春面发紫块，微肿麻木，至冬遍身色紫，不知痛痒，至春紫处俱大，至夏渐溃，又至春眉落指溃，此患在肝胆二经，令刺手指缝，并臂腿腕出黑血，先与再造散二眼，下毒秽，更以小柴胡合四物汤加白芷、防风、天麻、角刺，渐愈；又与换肌散。但遍体微赤，此血虚有火，因家贫未得调理，秋间发热，至春面仍发块，用前散并养血药，喜年少谨疾得愈。[114p]

The "Health Treasure Mirror" states: In the year of Wu-Yin, during the first month, a man named Duanku suffered from a severe wind illness, with extreme itching all over his face and neck. His eyebrows had fallen out, and applying hot soup provided some relief. He had to apply it several times day and night; even acupuncture provided some improvement. The venerable teacher said: The pulse of wind signifies a pathogenic wind. When the Wei and Ying (defensive and nutritive qi) become heated and cloudy, it damages the nasal bridge and discolors the skin. Severe wind indicates that wind and cold settle in the meridians and do not disperse. The treatment should involve needling the swollen areas with sharp needles to expel the harmful qi, stopping only when the swelling subsides. One should regularly consume prescribed food and avoid other foods.

The "Xue Ji Medical Cases" states: A man experienced bitterness in his mouth and tinnitus during winter, accompanied by itching and dampness in the scrotum. In spring, he developed purple spots on his face, slight swelling, and numbness, which progressed to widespread purple discoloration by winter, without any pain or itching. By spring, the purple areas grew larger, and in summer, they began to ulcerate; by spring, his eyebrows had fallen out and ulcers formed on his fingers. This illness was located in the liver and gallbladder meridians, and the treatment involved needling the spaces between his fingers, as well as on his arms and legs, drawing out dark blood. Initially, he was given "Zai Zao San" (Rebuilding Powder) two doses to clear the toxic filth, and then combined "Xiao Chai Hu Tang" (Minor Bupleurum Decoction) with "Si Wu Tang" (Four Substance Decoction), adding Bai Zhi, Fang Feng, Tian Ma, and Jiao Ci, which gradually improved his condition. He was also given "Huan Ji San" (Muscle Change Powder). However, he presented with slight redness all over, indicating a deficiency of blood with heat; due to financial difficulties, he had not received proper treatment. In autumn, he had fevers, and by spring, discoloration on his face persisted. With past formulas and blood-nourishing medicine, he gradually recovered, benefiting from the diligence of youth in managing his ailments.[114p]

　　一膏粱之人，鼻坏眉落，指脱体溃，热渴晡甚，用四物汤加酒炒黑黄蘗、知母、五味、麦门、白芷、天麻、角刺，三十余剂，热渴少止。时仲夏，精神倦怠，气喘身热，小便黄数，大便稀溏，此元气虚而时热胜也，用补中益气汤顿安。乃与换肌散及益气汤，兼服二月；更以生脉代茶饮，疮少退。时至仲秋，眩运少食，自汗体重，大便溏数，此亦时湿之证，用清燥汤调理而愈；又用补中益气汤少加酒炒黑黄蘗、知母、角刺、天麻，两月余而瘥。又因劳倦耳聩热渴，误服祛风散，病气益剧，身发赤疹，与益气聪明汤月许而愈。
　　一男子赤痛热渴，脓水淋漓，心烦掌热，目昧语濇，怔忡不宁，此心经受证也，用安神丸兼八珍汤，少加木通、炒黑黄连、远志，元气渐复；却行砭刺，外邪渐退；但便燥作渴，用柴胡饮八珍汤而愈，用换肌散而瘥。[115p]

A person accustomed to rich food had a nose gone bad and eyebrows fallen out, fingers detached and body decayed, suffering from intense heat and thirst. I prescribed a decoction of Four Substances Soup with wine, sautéed with black Phellodendron, Anemarrhena, Schisandra, Wheat, Angelica, Gastrodia, and Angelica sinensis—over thirty doses, with little relief for his thirst. It was mid-summer, and he felt weary, was short of breath and had a hot body, with yellow and frequent urination and loose stools. This was a case of depleted vital energy and excessive summer heat; therefore, I used the Emmeric Ziziphus Decoction for quick relief. I then prescribed the Muscle Exchange Powder and Energy Boosting Soup, taken together for two months; additionally, he replaced tea with the Shengmai Decoction, and his sores reduced. By mid-autumn, he experienced dizziness, little appetite, sweating, body heaviness, and frequent loose stools; this too was a symptom of dampness during the season. I used the Clear-Dry Decoction to regulate and heal him; moreover, using the Emmeric Ziziphus Decoction with a little wine, sautéing black Phellodendron, Anemarrhena, Gastrodia, and Angelica sinensis, it took over two months to recover. However, due to exhaustion and ear ringing, heat thirst, he mistakenly took a wind-dispelling powder, worsening his condition with red rashes on the body, which improved with the Energy and Clarity Decoction over a month until he recovered.

A man experienced red pain and thirst, with purulent discharge, agitation, hot palms, dim vision, and speech slurring, feeling anxious and uneasy—these were symptoms of heart organ damage. I prescribed a Spirit Calming Pill along with Eight Treasures Soup, adding a bit of Actinidia, roasted black Coptis, and Polygala; his vital energy gradually recovered. I applied acupuncture, and the external evil gradually retreated. However, he felt dryness leading to thirst; I used the Chaihu Decoction with Eight Treasures Soup for healing, followed by the Muscle Exchange Powder until he was cured.[115p]

　　一男子肚见青筋，面起紫泡，发热作渴，寅卯时甚，脉弦数，腿转筋，小便濇，此肝经火证，先用柴胡饮，热退便利；却用小柴胡合四物汤加龙胆草、炒山栀三十余剂，及八珍汤加柴胡、山栀，养其气血，乃用换肌散去其内毒而安。年余因劳役饮食失宜，寒热头痛，遍身赤疹，自用醉仙散而殁。
　　一男子面发紫疙瘩，脓水淋漓，睡中搐搦，遍身麻木，渐发赤块，劳怒则痒，肝脉洪大，砭刺臂腿腕各出血，用清胃汤加大黄、角刺四剂煎，下泻青丸，肝脉少退；以升麻汤数剂下前丸，诸证少愈；却用宝鉴换肌散斤许，又用小柴胡合四物汤加参、朮、天麻、角刺百余剂，及六味地黄丸半载而愈。后因劳遍身麻痒，脉微而迟，此气血俱虚，不能荣于腠理，用十全大补汤加五味、麦门，调理年余而安。[116p]

A man had blue veins in his abdomen, purple blisters on his face, felt feverish and thirsty, with symptoms worsening during the hours of Yin and Yang (early morning), a wiry and rapid pulse, leg cramps, and dark-colored urine. This indicated a condition of heat in the liver meridian. Initially, he was treated with Chai Hu Decoction, which reduced the heat and improved urination; then he was given Xiao Chai Hu Decoction combined with Si Wu Decoction, adding Gentian and fried Gardenia for over thirty doses, followed by Ba Zhen Decoction with Chai Hu and Gardenia to nourish his qi and blood, and finally used Huan Ji San to dispel internal toxins and stabilize his condition. After a year of labor and unsuitable diet, he suffered from headaches with alternating chills and fevers, and developed widespread rashes. He used Zui Xian San but unfortunately passed away.

Another man presented with purple nodules on his face, oozing pus, convulsions while sleeping, widespread numbness, and gradually developed red patches. He would itch upon exertion or anger. His liver pulse was large and forceful, and he had bleeding from cupping on his arms, legs, and wrists. He was treated with Qing Wei Decoction plus rhubarb and hornet's nest for four doses to induce a purgative effect, resulting in a slight decrease in liver pulse. A few doses of Sheng Ma Decoction followed to help expel the remaining issues, with marginal improvement. He then received Baojian Huan Ji San over the course of about a pound, along with Xiao Chai Hu Decoction combined with Si Wu Decoction adding ginseng, atractylodes, gastrodia, and hornet's nest for over one hundred doses, and he recovered after six months. Later, due to physical exertion, he experienced widespread itching, with a weak and slow pulse, indicating deficiency of both qi and blood that could not nourish the skin. He was treated with Shi Quan Da Bu Decoction adding five-flavored herb and wheat, and after a year of regulation, he was stable.[116p]

　　一男子面赤发紫泡，下体痒痛，午后发热，大便燥黑，此火盛而血虚也，用再造散及四物汤加防己、胆草，及刺腿指缝出毒血而便和；仍以前药加白朮、白芷、茯苓、羌活、独活而便黄；仍以四物去胆草、防己，少用独活，加元参、萆薢，五十余剂而疮退；却用补中益气汤加天麻、麦门而气血渐充。时仲秋霪雨，用清燥汤而安；随用换肌散、胡麻散、八珍汤兼服而愈。
　　一上舍面发肿，肌如癣，后变疙瘩色紫，搔之出水，此脾肺之证也，先用清胃汤以清胃热解表毒，又用四物汤加山栀、黄芩，柴胡、皂角刺、甘草节以养血祛风热；及砭臂腿腕手足指缝并患处，以去毒血，疏通隧道；乃与八珍汤加白芷、皂角刺、五加皮、全蝎及二圣散，兼服月余，以养阴血，治疮毒；又与补气泻荣汤少愈，再与换肌散而全愈。后因劳倦，遂发赤晕，日晡尤甚，以四物加丹皮、柴胡、山栀，并用补中益气汤年余，虽劳而不发。[117p]

A man presented with a red and purple face, itching and pain in the lower body, heat in the afternoon, and dry black stools. This indicated excessive fire and deficient blood. Treatment included Zai Zao San and Si Wu Tang, supplemented with Fang Ji and Dan Cao, to expel toxic blood through the toes, leading to improved bowel movements. The previous medications were then supplemented with Bai Zhu, Bai Zhi, Fu Ling, Qiang Huo, and Du Huo, resulting in yellow stools. Si Wu Tang was used again without Dan Cao and Fang Ji, with reduced use of Du Huo, and added Yuan Shen and Bi Xie. After more than fifty doses, the lesions receded. Later, a formula to tonify the middle and boost Qi with Tian Ma and Mai Men was administered to gradually restore Qi and blood. During the rainy late autumn, Qing Zao Tang was employed for comfort. Subsequently, Huan Ji San, Hu Ma San, and Ba Zhen Tang were taken together for recovery.

A patient in an upper chamber experienced facial swelling, skin resembling eczema, which later developed into purple lumps that leaked fluid when scratched, a manifestation of spleen and lung issues. Initially, Qing Wei Tang was used to clear stomach heat and resolve exterior toxins, followed by Si Wu Tang with Shan Zhi, Huang Qin, Chai Hu, Zao Jiao Ci, and Gan Cao to nourish the blood and dispel wind-heat. The affected areas of the arms, legs, wrists, hands, and toes were treated with acupuncture to remove toxic blood and clear channels. Lastly, Ba Zhen Tang was combined with Bai Zhi, Zao Jiao Ci, Wu Jia Pi, Quan Xie, and Er Sheng San for over a month to nourish Yin blood and address sores and toxins. There was slight improvement with Bu Qi Xie Rong Tang, followed by Huan Ji San for full recovery. However, due to overexertion, red rashes reappeared, particularly exacerbated in the afternoon, for which Si Wu Tang was adjusted with Dan Pi, Chai Hu, and Shan Zhi, alongside the Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang for over a year, allowing him to work without worsening his condition.[117p]

　　一男子遍身如癣，搔痒成疮，色紫麻木，掐之则痛，小便数而少，此脾胃受邪，证多在表，用清胃散，更砭刺患处并臂腿腕出黑血，神思渐爽；但恶寒体倦口干，此邪气去而真气虚也，以大剂参、芪、芎、归、蒺藜、桔梗数剂，元气顿复；却用八珍汤加黄芪、白芷、蒺藜、天麻、软柴胡及二圣散治之，其疮渐愈；后用换肌散、八珍汤等药，调理半载而痊。后仍发，误用克伐攻毒，患两感伤寒而死。
　　一男子遍身疙瘩，搔则不痒，掐则不痛，便闭作渴，此邪在内也，以再造散二服，微下三次；用桃仁承气汤加当归四剂，及砭恶血，渐知痛痒。但形体倦怠，用培养之剂，复其元气；又用二圣散，其疮顿愈；更用大补，年余而康。后患痰涎壅盛，舌强语濇，用二陈、苍朮、知、蘗、泽泻四剂而愈，再用补中益气汤调理而安。[118p]

A man was covered in sores like scabs, scratching them caused them to fester, his skin was purple and numb, pressing on them caused pain, and he had infrequent and scanty urination. This indicated an illness from the spleen and stomach, with the symptoms mainly on the surface. I used the Qingwei Powder and also needled the affected areas along with the arms and legs to draw out dark blood, which gradually improved his spirit; however, he still felt cold, fatigued, and had a dry mouth. This indicated that the evil qi had departed but genuine qi was deficient. I administered large doses of ginseng, astragalus, angelica, ligusticum, evodia, and platycodon, restoring his essential qi rapidly. Then I used the Eight Treasures Decoction with added astragalus, angelica, evodia, gastrodia, softened bupleurum, and the Two Holy Powder to treat him, which led to gradual recovery of the sores. Later, he had a recurrence but mistakenly used aggressive methods to attack the toxins, resulting in him suffering from both cold and warm pathogens and ultimately leading to death.

Another man had bumps all over his body; scratching did not cause itching, and pressing did not cause pain. He suffered from constipation and thirst; this indicated that the evil was internal. I prescribed the Zai Zao Powder twice, which slightly purged three times. I then used the Peaches and Plums Purging Decoction with four doses of angelica and needled to resolve the pathological blood, which gradually relieved the pain and itching. However, he felt fatigued, so I used tonifying medicine to restore his essential qi. Additionally, I used the Two Holy Powder, causing the sores to heal rapidly. I further applied substantial tonics, and after a year, he recovered. Later, he suffered from an accumulation of phlegm and sputum, with a stiff tongue and slurred speech. I used the Er Chen Decoction along with four doses of atractylodes, unhusked barley, and plantain, which led to his recovery, and then used the Bao Zhong Yi Qi Decoction to adjust and stabilize his condition.[118p]

　　一男子素清苦，眉尽落，病在肝胆二经也，乃刺臂腿腕及患处出黑血，空心服八珍汤加五味、胡麻、首乌、威灵仙，食后服换肌散。喜其无兼变之证，又能笃守禁忌，不半年而痊。
　　一儒者脚心或痒痛，或麻痒，或肿胀，二年后身体作痒，渐变疙瘩，发热耳鸣，日晡益甚，此属肾虚也，乃砭刺臂腿腕及手足指缝去其瘀血，用六味地黄丸料加五味、柴胡五十余剂以补肾，又用换肌散祛风丸以治疮，各斤许，疮渐愈，得滋补守禁而痊。
　　一上舍遍身患之，形病俱虚，余谓须用调补，元气完复，方治其疮。不信，恰服蛇酒以攻内毒，更敷砒霜等药以蚀外毒，顿加呕吐清水，体痛如锥。或以为毒气外发，余曰：脾主肌肉，此因毒药伤脾而然也。反服祛毒之剂，吐泻不止而死。
　　一男子用药熏洗，汗不止，喘嗽不食，腹鸣足冷，肢体抽搐，此因热伤元气，腠理不密，亡阳耳。是日果卒。
[119p]

A man lived in great distress; his eyebrows had completely fallen out, and he was ill from ailments affecting the liver and gallbladder. He pricked his arms, legs, and the afflicted areas to release black blood, taking Eight Treasures Decoction with added ingredients of five flavors, sesame, and Polygonum multiflorum. After eating, he took a medicinal powder to change the flesh. He was pleased that there were no complications and was able to strictly adhere to prescribed restrictions. In less than half a year, he recovered.

A Confucian scholar experienced itching and pain in the soles of his feet, or numbness and swelling. After two years, his body began to itch, gradually developing bumps, with heat and ringing in the ears that worsened in the afternoon; this was a sign of kidney deficiency. He treated it by pricking his arms, legs, and the spaces between his fingers to drain the stagnant blood, using a combination of Liuwei Dihuang pills with added five flavors and over fifty doses of Chaihu to tonify the kidneys. He also employed a powder to expel wind and treat sores, each weighing several jin. Gradually, the sores healed, as he received nourishment and adhered to restrictions.

A man in higher status was afflicted all over, his overall condition weak. I suggested he needed tonification to restore his vital energy before treating the sores. He did not believe this and instead consumed snake wine to attack internal toxins and applied arsenic and other medicines to corrode external toxins, which immediately led to vomiting of clear water and body pain like being pierced by a nail. Some thought the toxic gas was exiting his body; I pointed out that the spleen governs muscles, and this was due to the poison injuring the spleen. In contrast, taking detoxifying agents led to relentless vomiting and diarrhea, resulting in death.

Another man used a medicinal wash, and despite not sweating, suffered from wheezing, cough, loss of appetite, abdominal rumbling, cold extremities, and muscle spasms. This was caused by heat damaging vital energy, resulting in loose pores and loss of yang. That very day, he indeed died.[119p]
